If employer demand for labor rises faster than new workers enter to supply, price (wage) should rise. 		Private-sector nominal average hourly earnings growth 2.3-2.9% for abt 2.5 yrs. Last month: 3.1%. 		This month: *3.2%* growth over the year. Modest acceleration continues.
In manufacturing, workweek ticked up 0.1 hour to 40.9 hours, driven by 0.1 hour increase in overtime to 3.6 hrs. Compare to prior Decembers: 	2017: 40.7	2016: 40.7 	2015: 40.7 	2014: 41.0 	2013: 40.9	2012: 40.7
That‚Äôs the extensive quantity (Q) margin. Intensive Q margin is average hours		Average workweek hours for private sector ticked up 0.1 hr to 34.5 = a year ago. 34.6 2 yrs ago. 		Frontline (prod &amp; nonsupervisory) workers stable 33.7 hrs = last 2 months	Dec'17: 33.8	Dec'16: 33.6
Employment-population ratio (EPOP) stable, at 60.6%, stable for 3 months, up 0.4% over the year. Has had that same trend over 5 prior years to last month.
Labor force participation rate (LFPR) up to 63.1%. LFPR has been pretty flat; was 62.7% a year ago &amp; 2 years ago &amp; 3 years ago. Boomer retirements push LFPR down 0.25-0.3 pp/yr. So staying still is a kind of progress.
